2025-12-11 15:58:36.968 | INFO     | metagpt.actions.write_prd:run:86 - New requirement detected: # Prompt: Create a snake game in Python
## Requirements:
### Game Board:
- Create a grid-based game board.
- Define the dimensions of the grid (e.g., 10x10).
- Display the grid on the screen.
### Snake Initialization:
- Place the snake on the game board.
- Define the initial length and starting position of the snake.
- Choose a direction for the snake to start moving immediately, without user input (e.g., right).
### Snake Movement:
- Implement arrow key controls for snake movement.
- Ensure the snake moves continuously in the chosen direction.
- Update the snake’s position on the grid.
### Food Generation:
- Generate food at random positions on the game board.
- Ensure food doesn’t appear on the snake’s body.
### Collision Handling:
- Detect collisions between the snake and the game board boundaries.
- Detect collisions between the snake’s head and its body.
- Detect collisions between the snake’s head and the food.
### Snake Growth:
- Increase the length of the snake when it consumes food, adding a new segment to the snake’s body.
### Score Display:
- Implement a scoring system.
- Display the current score on the screen.
### Game Over Condition:
- Trigger a game over scenario when the snake collides with the boundaries.
- Trigger a game over scenario when the snake collides with its own body.
- Display a game over message.
- Allow the player to restart the game.
### Graphics and User Interface:
- Use graphics or ASCII characters to represent the snake and food.
- Design a user-friendly interface with clear instructions.
### Animations and Effects:
- Add animations for snake movement and growth.
- Implement visual effects for collisions and food consumption.

  def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. power-ups."}\n\n## Legacy Code\n```Code\n----- board.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Board class with methods for drawing the board and checking collisions.\n\nAttributes:\n    width (int): The width of the board.\n    height (int): The height of the board.\n    screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\n\nclass Board:\n    """\n    A class representing the game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # the board.\n    height (int): The height of the board.\n    screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\n\nclass Board:\n    """\n    A class representing the game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Move the snake\n        new_head_x, new_head_y = snake_body[0]\n        new_head_x += 20\n        snake_body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        snake_body.pop()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if board.check_collision(snake_body):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n\n\n## Code to be Reviewed: snake.py\n```Code\n"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: \'Board\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        return (head_x, head_y) == (food.x, food.y)\n\n    def update_direction(self, direction: str) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            direction (str): The new direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        """\n        if direction in [\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', \'right\']:\n            self.direction = direction\n\n```\n\n\n\n# Format example 1\n## Code Review: snake.py\n1. game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Move the snake\n        new_head_x, new_head_y = snake_body[0]\n        new_head_x += 20\n        snake_body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        snake_body.pop()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if board.check_collision(snake_body):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n\n\n## Code to be Reviewed: snake.py\n```Code\n"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: \'Board\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        return (head_x, head_y) == (food.x, food.y)\n\n    def update_direction(self, direction: str) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            direction (str): The new direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        """\n        if direction in [\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', \'right\'] and direction != self.get_opposite_direction():\n            self.direction = direction\n\n    def get_opposite_direction(self) -> str:\n        """\n        Gets the opposite direction of the snake\'s current direction.\n\n        Returns:\n            str: The opposite direction of the snake.\n        """\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            return \'down\'\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            return \'up\'\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            return \'right\'\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            return \'left\'\n\n    def handle_user_input(self, event: pygame.event.Event) -> None:\n        """\n        Handles user input to change the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            event (pygame.event.Event): The Pygame event object.\n        """\n        if event.type == pygame.KEYDOWN:\n            if event.key == pygame.K_UP and self.direction != \'down\':\n                self.update_direction(\'up\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_DOWN and self.direction != \'up\':\n                self.update_direction(\'down\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_LEFT and self.direction != \'right\':\n                self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n            snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n        # Move the snake\n Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # power-ups."}\n\n## Code Files\n----- board.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Board class with methods for drawing the board and checking collisions.\n\nAttributes:\n    width (int): The width of the board.\n    height (int): The height of the board.\n    screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\n\nclass Board:\n    """\n    A class representing the game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Move the snake\n        new_head_x, new_head_y = snake_body[0]\n        new_head_x += 20\n        snake_body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        snake_body.pop()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if board.check_collision(snake_body):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n----- snake.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: Board) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        return (head_x, head_y) == (food.x, food.y)\n\n    def update_direction(self, direction: str) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            direction (str): The new direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        """\n        if direction in [\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', \'right\'] and direction != self.get_opposite_direction():\n            self.direction = direction\n\n    def get_opposite_direction(self) -> str:\n        """\n        Gets the opposite direction of the snake\'s current direction.\n\n        Returns:\n            str: The opposite direction of the snake.\n        """\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            return \'down\'\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            return \'up\'\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            return \'right\'\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            return \'left\'\n\n    def handle_user_input(self, event: pygame.event.Event) -> None:\n        """\n        Handles user input to change the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            event (pygame.event.Event): The Pygame event object.\n        """\n        if event.type == pygame.KEYDOWN:\n            if event.key == pygame.K_UP and self.direction != \'down\':\n                self.update_direction(\'up\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_DOWN and self.direction != \'up\':\n                self.update_direction(\'down\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_LEFT and self.direction != \'right\':\n                self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import sys\n    pygame.init()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    board = Board()\n    snake = Snake()\n\n    running = True\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n            snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n        # Move the snake\n        snake.move()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if snake.check_collision(board):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the display\n        board.update_display(snake.body)\n        pygame.display.flip()\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n    sys.exit()\n```\n\n\n## Code to be Reviewed: food.py\n```Code\n"""\nThis module contains the Food class with methods for generating food and checking food collisions.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n"""\n\nimport random\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Food:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s food.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, board: Board):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Food instance.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n        """\n        self.board = board\n        self.x = 0\n        self.y = 0\n        self.generate()\n\n    def generate(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Generates a new food position on the board.\n\n        This method randomly selects an empty space on the board as the new food position.\n        """\n        while True:\n            self.x = random.randint(0, self.board.width - 20) // 20 * 20\n            self.y = random.randint(0, self.board.height - 20) // 20 * 20\n            if (self.x, self.y) not in [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]:\n                break\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the food collides with the snake.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        return (self.x, self.y) in snake_body\n\n    def draw(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Draws the food on the board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a red square representing the food.\n        """\n        pygame.draw.rect(self.board.screen, (255, 0, 0), (self.x, self.y, 20, 20))\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import pygame\n    from board import Board\n\n    pygame.init()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    board = Board()\n    food = Food(board)\n\n    running = True\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Draw the board and food\n        board.draw()\n        food.draw()\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n\n```\n\n\n\n# Format example 1\n## Code Review: food.py\n1. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: Board) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food      self.direction = direction\n\n    def get_opposite_direction(self) -> str:\n        """\n        Gets the opposite direction of the snake\'s current direction.\n\n        Returns:\n            str: The opposite direction of the snake.\n        """\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            return \'down\'\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            return \'up\'\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            return \'right\'\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            return \'left\'\n\n    def handle_user_input(self, event: pygame.event.Event) -> None:\n        """\n        Handles user input to change the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            event (pygame.event.Event): The Pygame event object.\n        """\n        if event.type == pygame.KEYDOWN:\n            if event.key == pygame.K_UP and self.direction != \'down\':\n                self.update_direction(\'up\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_DOWN and self.direction != \'up\':\n                self.update_direction(\'down\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_LEFT and self.direction != \'right\':\n                self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n            snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n        # Move the snake\n        snake.move()\n\n Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n----- snake.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: Board) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        return (head_x, head_y) == (food.x, food.y)\n\n    def update_direction(self, direction: str) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            direction (str): The new direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        """\n        if direction in [\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', \'right\'] and direction != self.get_opposite_direction():\n            self.direction = direction\n\n    def get_opposite_direction(self) -> str:\n        """\n        Gets the opposite direction of the snake\'s current direction.\n\n        Returns:\n            str: The opposite direction of the snake.\n        """\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            return \'down\'\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            return \'up\'\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            return \'right\'\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            return \'left\'\n\n    def handle_user_input(self, event: pygame.event.Event) -> None:\n        """\n        Handles user input to change the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            event (pygame.event.Event): The Pygame event object.\n        """\n        if event.type == pygame.KEYDOWN:\n            if event.key == pygame.K_UP and self.direction != \'down\':\n                self.update_direction(\'up\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_DOWN and self.direction != \'up\':\n                self.update_direction(\'down\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_LEFT and self.direction != \'right\':\n                self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import sys\n    pygame.init()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    board = Board()\n    snake = Snake()\n\n    running = True\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n            snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n        # Move the snake\n        snake.move()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if snake.check_collision(board):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the display\n        board.update_display(snake.body)\n        pygame.display.flip()\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n    sys.exit()\n```\n----- food.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Food class with methods for generating food, checking food collisions, and updating its position.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n    board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n"""\n\nimport random\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Food:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s food.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n        board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, board: Board):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Food instance.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n        """\n        self.board = board\n        self.x = 0\n        self.y = 0\n        self.generate()\n\n    def generate(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Generates a new food position on the board.\n\n        This method randomly selects an empty space on the board as the new food position, ensuring it does not overlap with the snake\'s body.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        while True:\n            self.x = random.randint(0, self.board.width - 20) // 20 * 20\n            self.y = random.randint(0, self.board.height - 20) // 20 * 20\n            # Check if the generated position overlaps with the snake\'s body\n            if (self.x, self.y) not in snake_body:\n                break\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_head: tuple) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the food collides with the snake.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_head (tuple): The x and y coordinates of the snake\'s head.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        return (self.x, self.y) == snake_head\n\n    def draw(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Draws the food on the board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a red square representing the food.\n        """\n        pygame.draw.rect(self.board.screen, (255, 0, 0), (self.x, self.y, 20, 20))\n\n    def update_position(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the food\'s position after being consumed by the snake.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        self.generate(snake_body)\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import pygame\n    from board import Board\n\n    pygame.init()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    board = Board()\n    food = Food(board)\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n\n    running = True\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Draw the board and food\n        board.draw()\n        food.draw()\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n```\n\n## Debug logs\n```text\n\n\n\n```\n\n## Bug Feedback the board.\n    height (int): The height of the board.\n    screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\n\nclass Board:\n    """\n    A class representing the game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Move the snake\n        new_head_x, new_head_y = snake_body[0]\n        new_head_x += 20\n        snake_body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        snake_body.pop()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if board.check_collision(snake_body):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n----- snake.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == the board.\n    height (int): The height of the board.\n    screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\n\nclass Board:\n    """\n    A class representing the game board.\n\n    Attributes:\n        width (int): The width of the board.\n        height (int): The height of the board.\n        screen (pygame.display.set_mode): The Pygame screen object.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, width: int = 800, height: int = 600):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Board instance.\n\n        Args:\n            width (int, optional): The width of the board. Defaults to 800.\n            height (int, optional): The height of the board. Defaults to 600.\n        """\n        self.width = width\n        self.height = height\n        pygame.init()\n        self.screen = pygame.display.set_mode((self.width, self.height))\n\n    def draw(self):\n        """\n        Draws the game board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a grid on the screen.\n        """\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_body: list) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake\'s position is outside the board or if it collides with itself.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        head_x, head_y = snake_body[0]\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= self.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= self.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in snake_body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def update_game_state(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the game state after a move.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        # Clear the screen\n        self.screen.fill((255, 255, 255))\n\n        # Draw grid lines\n        for i in range(0, self.width, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (i, 0), (i, self.height))\n        for i in range(0, self.height, 20):\n            pygame.draw.line(self.screen, (200, 200, 200), (0, i), (self.width, i))\n\n        # Draw the snake\'s body\n        for x, y in snake_body:\n            pygame.draw.rect(self.screen, (0, 255, 0), (x, y, 20, 20))\n\n        pygame.display.flip()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    board = Board()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    running = True\n    snake_body = [(100, 100), (120, 100), (140, 100)]\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n\n        # Move the snake\n        new_head_x, new_head_y = snake_body[0]\n        new_head_x += 20\n        snake_body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        snake_body.pop()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if board.check_collision(snake_body):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the game state\n        board.update_game_state(snake_body)\n\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n```\n----- snake.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Snake class with methods for moving the snake, checking collisions, and growing the snake.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n    direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n    length (int): The current length of the snake.\n"""\n\nimport pygame\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Snake:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s snake.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the snake.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the snake.\n        direction (str): The current direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        length (int): The current length of the snake.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, x: int = 100, y: int = 100):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Snake instance.\n\n        Args:\n            x (int, optional): The initial x-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n            y (int, optional): The initial y-coordinate of the snake. Defaults to 100.\n        """\n        self.x = x\n        self.y = y\n        self.direction = \'right\'\n        self.length = 1\n        self.body = [(x, y)]\n\n    def move(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Moves the snake in its current direction.\n\n        This method updates the snake\'s position based on its current direction.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y - 20\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x, head_y + 20\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x - 20, head_y\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            new_head_x, new_head_y = head_x + 20, head_y\n\n        self.body.insert(0, (new_head_x, new_head_y))\n        if len(self.body) > self.length:\n            self.body.pop()\n\n    def grow(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Increases the length of the snake.\n\n        This method increments the snake\'s length by one unit.\n        """\n        self.length += 1\n\n    def check_collision(self, board: Board) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the board or itself.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        # Check if the snake is outside the board\n        if head_x < 0 or head_x >= board.width or head_y < 0 or head_y >= board.height:\n            return True\n\n        # Check if the snake collides with itself\n        for body_part in self.body[1:]:\n            if body_part == (head_x, head_y):\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_food_collision(self, food: \'Food\') -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the snake collides with the food.\n\n        Args:\n            food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        head_x, head_y = self.body[0]\n        return (head_x, head_y) == (food.x, food.y)\n\n    def update_direction(self, direction: str) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            direction (str): The new direction of the snake (\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', or \'right\').\n        """\n        if direction in [\'up\', \'down\', \'left\', \'right\'] and direction != self.get_opposite_direction():\n            self.direction = direction\n\n    def get_opposite_direction(self) -> str:\n        """\n        Gets the opposite direction of the snake\'s current direction.\n\n        Returns:\n            str: The opposite direction of the snake.\n        """\n        if self.direction == \'up\':\n            return \'down\'\n        elif self.direction == \'down\':\n            return \'up\'\n        elif self.direction == \'left\':\n            return \'right\'\n        elif self.direction == \'right\':\n            return \'left\'\n\n    def handle_user_input(self, event: pygame.event.Event) -> None:\n        """\n        Handles user input to change the snake\'s direction.\n\n        Args:\n            event (pygame.event.Event): The Pygame event object.\n        """\n        if event.type == pygame.KEYDOWN:\n            if event.key == pygame.K_UP and self.direction != \'down\':\n                self.update_direction(\'up\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_DOWN and self.direction != \'up\':\n                self.update_direction(\'down\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_LEFT and self.direction != \'right\':\n                self.update_direction(\'left\')\n            elif event.key == pygame.K_RIGHT and self.direction != \'left\':\n                self.update_direction(\'right\')\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    import sys\n    pygame.init()\n    clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n    board = Board()\n    snake = Snake()\n\n    running = True\n    while running:\n        for event in pygame.event.get():\n            if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                running = False\n            snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n        # Move the snake\n        snake.move()\n\n        # Check for collisions\n        if snake.check_collision(board):\n            print("Game Over")\n            running = False\n\n        # Update the display\n        board.update_display(snake.body)\n        pygame.display.flip()\n        clock.tick(10)\n\n    pygame.quit()\n    sys.exit()\n```\n----- food.py\n```"""\nThis module contains the Food class with methods for generating food, checking food collisions, and updating its position.\n\nAttributes:\n    x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n    y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n    board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n"""\n\nimport random\nfrom board import Board\n\nclass Food:\n    """\n    A class representing the game\'s food.\n\n    Attributes:\n        x (int): The initial x-coordinate of the food.\n        y (int): The initial y-coordinate of the food.\n        board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self, board: Board):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Food instance.\n\n        Args:\n            board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n        """\n        self.board = board\n        self.x = 0\n        self.y = 0\n        self.generate()\n\n    def generate(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Generates a new food position on the board.\n\n        This method randomly selects an empty space on the board as the new food position, ensuring it does not overlap with the snake\'s body.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_body (list): A list of tuples representing the x and y coordinates of the snake\'s body parts.\n        """\n        while True:\n            self.x = random.randint(0, self.board.width - 20) // 20 * 20\n            self.y = random.randint(0, self.board.height - 20) // 20 * 20\n            # Check if the generated position overlaps with the snake\'s body\n            if (self.x, self.y) not in snake_body:\n                break\n\n    def check_collision(self, snake_head: tuple) -> bool:\n        """\n        Checks if the food collides with the snake.\n\n        Args:\n            snake_head (tuple): The x and y coordinates of the snake\'s head.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if a collision occurred, False otherwise.\n        """\n        return (self.x, self.y) == snake_head\n\n    def draw(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Draws the food on the board.\n\n        This method uses Pygame to draw a red square representing the food.\n        """\n        pygame.draw.rect(self.board.screen, (255, 0, 0), (self.x, self.y, 20, 20))\n\n    def update_position(self, snake_body: list) -> None:\n        """\n        Updates the food\'s position after being consumed by the snake.\n\n        Args:\n contains the Game class with methods for running the game, drawing the board, and handling user input.\n\nAttributes:\n    board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n    snake (Snake): The game\'s representing the game.\n\n    Attributes:\n        board (Board): The game\'s board instance.\n        snake (Snake): The game\'s snake instance.\n        food (Food): The game\'s food instance.\n    """\n\n    def __init__(self):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Game instance.\n        """\n        self.board = Board()\n        self.snake = Snake()\n        self.food = Food(self.board)\n\n    def run(self) -> None:\n        """\n        Runs the game.\n\n        This method initializes the Pygame window, sets up the game loop, and handles user input.\n        """\n        pygame.init()\n        clock = pygame.time.Clock()\n\n        running = True\n        while running:\n            for event in pygame.event.get():\n                if event.type == pygame.QUIT:\n                    running = False\n                self.snake.handle_user_input(event)\n\n            # Move the snake\n            self.snake.move()\n\n            # Check for collisions with the board or itself\n            if self.snake.check_collision(self.board):\n                print("Game Over")\n                running = False\n\n            # Check for collision with food\n            if self.snake.check_food_collision(self.food):\n                self.snake.grow()\n                self.food.generate(self.snake.body)\n\n            # Update the display\n            self.board.screen.fill((0, 0, 0))  # Fill the screen with black color\n            for x in range(0, self.board.width, 20):\n                pygame.draw.line(self.board.screen, (40, 40, 40), (x, 0), (x, self.board.height))\n            for y in range(0, self.board.height, 20):\n                pygame.draw.line(self.board.screen, (40, 40, 40), (0, y), (self.board.width, y))\n            self.food.draw()\n            for pos in self.snake.body:\n                pygame.draw.rect(self.board.screen, (0, 255, 0), (pos[0], pos[1], 20, 20))\n            pygame.display.flip()\n            clock.tick(10)\n\n        pygame.quit()\n\n# Example usage:\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    game = Game()\n    game.run()\n\n```\n\n\n\n# Format example 1\n## Code Review: game.py\n1.
